                        Great resume. I think the important stuff is all covered already.

I have comments on less-important stuff. These aren't hard rules, just ideas for consideration:

- If the content can be adjusted to fit all on one page, it should be. So, to do this... 

- "AWS Joe Mama's Diner" currently in the skills and tools section indicates this comes from the Ursula Lopez resume sample, and can be trimmed out. There might be other skills and tools to trim out as well. My hope is that after trimming the list, there number of lines consumed will be reduced.

- Change the margins to around 0.5" on each side. This should help squeeze everything onto one page. This change will also make this resume more closely match the resume template.

- Keep the number of projects to the 2-3 most important. Removing the 4th project will free up space. Hopefully with these changes, the resume will be one page.

- I passed the personal statement through grammarly and made a few changes. You're welcome to use this: "Dedicated and experienced IT professional with excellent programming skills in multiple programming languages. Possesses a comprehensive understanding of computer architecture, operating systems, and data structures. Security Clearance Status: SSBI favorable. Fluent in English and Chinese Mandarin."

- Add year degrees/certificates were obtained to Education section.

- Remove "https://" and "www." from all links. eg: "linkedin.com/in/rui-guo", "github.com/mvrk", "github.com/TheSnorelaxClan", etc.

- Put the location after the school/institution name in the education section. eg: "Software Development in JavaScript and Python, Code Fellows, Seattle, WA". Add locations to LSU and Hainan University too, even though the location is in the name of them.

- Use the following date format, including the space around the dash. Change "01/2015-05/2019" to "Jan 2015 - May 2019".

                      Jul 18 at 1:22pm

                        This is 10/10 points I think. See rubric below.

I'm going to be really detailed to start out with. The hope is that the things I point out will be increasingly familiar very rapidly. So don't worry, it's just meant to help learn faster, and if you have any thoughts feel free to let me know:

- This is a tiny thing, but one of the assignment requirements is to match the format exactly. There should be a line break before and after the acknowledgements to the user inputs.

- Typing quit correctly ends the order; however, there's a little bug. When "quit" is entered, it's added to the order list just before the loop ends. "** 1 order of quit have been added to your meal **"

- Git commit messages could be more informative about why a change is being made. For example, one commit message could be, "Add: prints intro", another could be, "Add: prompt user to order", or "Fix: acknowledgment line breaks".

The benefit of commit messages like this is that a history of changes can be seen, and any commit can be looked at to isolate the code changes for a specific feature change.

- Readme exists, though is currently blank. There's a template to follow for readme's on the submission instructions page.

- "lab1" folder I think is the ".venv" folder. When creating the virtual environment, make sure the command being used is "python .venv venv", and then it with "source .venv/bin/activate". This way the gitignore will notice there's a ".venv" folder and prevent the venv stuff from being uploaded to github.

Checklist:

Features:

- [✓] Prints intro.
- [✓] Prints menu.
- [✓] Menu includes appetizers, entrees, desserts, beverages.
- [✓] Prompts to enter an order.
- [✓] Acknowledgement after input provided to prompt.
- [✓] Instructions provided to exit.
- [ ] Matches sample format exactly.
- [ ] No bugs.

Submission Instructions

- [✓] Submission links to readme corresponding to assignment's branch.
- [✓] File tree matches instructions.
- [✓] .gitignore exists and includes .venv.
- [ ] .venv exists locally only and is not uploaded to github.
- [ ] Readme matches template structure.

Rubric

- [5/6] Assignment requirements.
- [3/3] Idiomatic style.
- [0.5/1] Git workflow.
- [2/2] Adjustments for lateness or effort.
- [0/2] Bonus for stretch goals. Note: grade caps at 10/10 points.
                      
                      
                    
                    
                      Chloe Nott,
                      Jul 19 at 6:43am

                        The drawing/whiteboard looks good though.

My usual comments for informational purposes:

- Wrap the code in a function. Some code challenges will consistent of multiple functions in the future. Plus it's a good way to communicate the inputs (parameters) and output (return).

- Time complexity is O(N) because of how list slicing is implemented in python. You have the right idea with it being a single pointer so it seems like it should just be an O(1) break and splice.

See documentation for get slice: 

https://wiki.python.org/moin/TimeComplexity

- Space complexity is also O(N) because the newArray occupies extra space equal to the input array.

- Code redundancy can be improved by putting only "m = arrayToBeDivided[].length / 2" inside the conditional, and nothing else.
                      
                      
                    
                    
                      Chloe Nott,

    def find_maximum_value(self):

                        This is 10/10 points I think. See rubric below.

I'm going to be really detailed to start out with. The hope is that the things I point out will be increasingly familiar very rapidly. So don't worry, it's just meant to help learn faster, and if you have any thoughts feel free to let me know:

- This is a tiny thing, but one of the assignment requirements is to match the format exactly. There should be a line break before and after the acknowledgements to the user inputs.

- Typing quit correctly ends the order; however, there's a little bug. When "quit" is entered, it's added to the order list just before the loop ends. "** 1 order of quit have been added to your meal **"

- Git commit messages could be more informative about why a change is being made. For example, one commit message could be, "Add: prints intro", another could be, "Add: prompt user to order", or "Fix: acknowledgment line breaks".

The benefit of commit messages like this is that a history of changes can be seen, and any commit can be looked at to isolate the code changes for a specific feature change.

- Readme exists, though is currently blank. There's a template to follow for readme's on the submission instructions page.

- "lab1" folder I think is the ".venv" folder. When creating the virtual environment, make sure the command being used is "python .venv venv", and then it with "source .venv/bin/activate". This way the gitignore will notice there's a ".venv" folder and prevent the venv stuff from being uploaded to github.

Checklist:

Features:

- [✓] Prints intro.
- [✓] Prints menu.
- [✓] Menu includes appetizers, entrees, desserts, beverages.
- [✓] Prompts to enter an order.
- [✓] Acknowledgement after input provided to prompt.
- [✓] Instructions provided to exit.
- [ ] Matches sample format exactly.
- [ ] No bugs.

Submission Instructions

- [✓] Submission links to readme corresponding to assignment's branch.
- [✓] File tree matches instructions.
- [✓] .gitignore exists and includes .venv.
- [ ] .venv exists locally only and is not uploaded to github.
- [ ] Readme matches template structure.

Rubric

- [5/6] Assignment requirements.
- [3/3] Idiomatic style.
- [0.5/1] Git workflow.
- [2/2] Adjustments for lateness or effort.
- [0/2] Bonus for stretch goals. Note: grade caps at 10/10 points.

                        The drawing/whiteboard looks good though.

My usual comments for informational purposes:

- Wrap the code in a function. Some code challenges will consistent of multiple functions in the future. Plus it's a good way to communicate the inputs (parameters) and output (return).

- Time complexity is O(N) because of how list slicing is implemented in python. You have the right idea with it being a single pointer so it seems like it should just be an O(1) break and splice.

See documentation for get slice: 

https://wiki.python.org/moin/TimeComplexity

- Space complexity is also O(N) because the newArray occupies extra space equal to the input array.

- Code redundancy can be improved by putting only "m = arrayToBeDivided[].length / 2" inside the conditional, and nothing else.

    def find_maximum_value(self):
